                10.1038/ncomms4529</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar%3Fhl%3Den%26q%3DLin%252C%2BF.%253B%2BMarkus%252C%2BI.%2BM.%253B%2BNordlund%252C%2BD.%253B%2BWeng%252C%2BT.%2BC.%253B%2BAsta%252C%2BM.%2BD.%253B%2BXin%252C%2BH.%2BL.%253B%2BDoeff%252C%2BM.%2BM.Nat.%2BCommun.%2B2014%252C%2B5%252C%2B3529%25E2%2580%25933527&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.7b01366&amp;doiOfLink=10.1038%2Fncomms4529&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Surface reconstruction and chemical evolution of stoichiometric layered cathode materials for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lin Feng; Doeff Marca M; Markus Isaac M; Nordlund Dennis; Weng Tsu-Chien; Asta Mark D; Xin Huolin L</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3529</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">The present study sheds light on the long-standing challenges associated with high-voltage operation of LiNi(x)Mn(x)Co(1-2x)O2 cathode materials for lithium-ion batteries.  Using correlated ensemble-averaged high-throughput X-ray absorption spectroscopy and spatially resolved electron microscopy and spectroscopy, here we report structural reconstruction (formation of a surface reduced layer, to transition) and chemical evolution (formation of a surface reaction layer) at the surface of LiNi(x)Mn(x)Co(1-2x)O2 particles.  These are primarily responsible for the prevailing capacity fading and impedance buildup under high-voltage cycling conditions, as well as the first-cycle coulombic inefficiency.  It was found that the surface reconstruction exhibits a strong anisotropic characteristic, which predominantly occurs along lithium diffusion channels.  Furthermore, the surface reaction layer is composed of lithium fluoride embedded in a complex organic matrix.  This work sets a refined example for the study of surface reconstruction and chemical evolution in battery materials using combined diagnostic tools at complementary length scales.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref22" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1039/C4EE02986K"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ding, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cui, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Karpuzov, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tan, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kohandehghan, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mitlin, D.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Energy Environ. Sci.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">8</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">941</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">955</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

The durability, high power, energy efficiency, and low cost needed for grid-scale storage pose substantial challenges for conventional battery technol.  Here, we demonstrate insertion/extn. of sodium and potassium ions in a low-strain nickel hexacyanoferrate electrode material for at least five thousand deep cycles at high current densities in inexpensive aq. electrolytes.  Its open-framework structure allows retention of 66% of the initial capacity even at a high (41.7C) rate.  At low current densities, its round trip energy efficiency reaches 99%.  This low-cost material is readily synthesized in bulk quantities.  The long cycle life, high power, good energy efficiency, safety, and inexpensive prodn. method make nickel hexacyanoferrate an attractive candidate for use in large-scale batteries to support the elec. grid.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref32" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2016.08.010"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ren, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yao, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Niu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zheng, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">An, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wei, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yan, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mai, L.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nano Energy</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">28</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">216</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">223</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                10.1038/nmat2612</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar%3Fhl%3Den%26q%3DBrezesinski%252C%2BT.%253B%2BWang%252C%2BJ.%253B%2BTolbert%252C%2BS.%2BH.%253B%2BDunn%252C%2BB.Nat.%2BMater.%2B2010%252C%2B9%252C%2B146%25E2%2580%2593151&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.7b01366&amp;doiOfLink=10.1038%2Fnmat2612&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ordered mesoporous α-MoO3 with iso-oriented nanocrystalline walls for thin-film pseudocapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Brezesinski, Torsten; Wang, John; Tolbert, Sarah H.; Dunn, Bruce</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2010</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">146-151</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NMAACR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1476-1122</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Capacitive energy storage is distinguished from other types of electrochem. energy storage by short charging times and the ability to deliver significantly more power than batteries.  A limitation to this technol. is its low energy d. and there is interest in exploring pseudo-capacitive materials where faradaic mechanisms offer increased energy storage.  The capacitive charge-storage properties of mesoporous films of iso-oriented α-MoO3 are superior to those of either mesoporous amorphous material or nonporous cryst. MoO3.  Whereas both cryst. and amorphous mesoporous materials show redox pseudo-capacitance, the iso-oriented layered cryst. domains enable Li ions to be inserted into the van der Waals gaps of the α-MoO3.  Probably this extra contribution arises from an intercalation pseudo-capacitance, which occurs on the same timescale as redox pseudo-capacitance.  The result is increased charge-storage capacity without compromising charge/discharge kinetics in mesoporous cryst. MoO3.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref37" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1038/nmat3601"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Augustyn, V.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Come, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lowe, M. A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kim, J. W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Taberna, P. L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tolbert, S. H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Abruña, H.                 10.1038/nmat3601</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar%3Fhl%3Den%26q%3DAugustyn%252C%2BV.%253B%2BCome%252C%2BJ.%253B%2BLowe%252C%2BM.%2BA.%253B%2BKim%252C%2BJ.%2BW.%253B%2BTaberna%252C%2BP.%2BL.%253B%2BTolbert%252C%2BS.%2BH.%253B%2BAbru%25C3%25B1a%252C%2BH.%2BD.%253B%2BSimon%252C%2BP.%253B%2BDunn%252C%2BB.Nat.%2BMater.%2B2013%252C%2B12%252C%2B518%25E2%2580%2593522&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.7b01366&amp;doiOfLink=10.1038%2Fnmat3601&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-rate electrochemical energy storage through Li+ intercalation pseudocapacitance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Augustyn, Veronica; Come, Jeremy; Lowe, Michael A.; Kim, Jong Woung; Taberna, Pierre-Louis; Tolbert, Sarah H.; Abruna, Hector D.; Simon, Patrice; Dunn, Bruce</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">518-522</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NMAACR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1476-1122</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pseudocapacitance is commonly assocd. with surface or near-surface reversible redox reactions, as obsd. with RuO2·xH2O in an acidic electrolyte.  However, we recently demonstrated that a pseudocapacitive mechanism occurs when lithium ions are inserted into mesoporous and nanocrystal films of orthorhombic Nb2O5 (T-Nb2O5; refs , ).  Here, we quantify the kinetics of charge storage in T-Nb2O5: currents that vary inversely with time, charge-storage capacity that is mostly independent of rate, and redox peaks that exhibit small voltage offsets even at high rates.  We also define the structural characteristics necessary for this process, termed intercalation pseudocapacitance, which are a cryst. network that offers two-dimensional transport pathways and little structural change on intercalation.  The principal benefit realized from intercalation pseudocapacitance is that high levels of charge storage are achieved within short periods of time because there are no limitations from solid-state diffusion.  Thick electrodes (up to 40 μm thick) prepd. with T-Nb2O5 offer the promise of exploiting intercalation pseudocapacitance to obtain high-rate charge-storage devices.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref38" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2011.08.015"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huang, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ren, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, W.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                 10.1016/j.jpowsour.2011.08.015</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar%3Fhl%3Den%26q%3DWang%252C%2BH.%253B%2BHuang%252C%2BK.%253B%2BRen%252C%2BY.%253B%2BHuang%252C%2BX.%253B%2BLiu%252C%2BS.%253B%2BWang%252C%2BW.J.%2BPower%2BSources%2B2011%252C%2B196%252C%2B9786%25E2%2580%25939791&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.7b01366&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jpowsour.2011.08.015&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Ever-growing energy needs and depleting fossil-fuel resources demand the pursuit of sustainable energy alternatives, including both renewable energy sources and sustainable storage technologies.  It is therefore essential to incorporate material abundance, eco-efficient synthetic processes and life-cycle anal. into the design of new electrochem. storage systems.  At present, a few existing technologies address these issues, but in each case, fundamental and technol. hurdles remain to be overcome.  Here the authors provide an overview of the current state of energy storage from a sustainability perspective.  The authors introduce the notion of sustainability through discussion of the energy and environmental costs of state-of-the-art Li-ion batteries, considering elemental abundance, toxicity, synthetic methods and scalability.  With the same themes in mind, the authors also highlight current and future electrochem. storage systems beyond Li-ion batteries.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Developing high-performance nonprecious-metal electrocatalysts for the oxygen redn. reaction (ORR) is crucial for a variety of renewable energy conversion and storage systems. B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Park, K. S.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Am. Chem. Soc.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">135</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">1167</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">1176</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/ja3091438</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">7</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The Li-Ion Rechargeable Battery: A Perspective</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Goodenough, John B.; Park, Kyu-Sung</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">135</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1167-1176</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JACSAT</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0002-7863</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Each cell of a battery stores elec. energy as chem. energy in two electrodes, a reductant (anode) and an oxidant (cathode), sepd. by an electrolyte that transfers the ionic component of the chem. reaction inside the cell and forces the electronic component outside the battery.  The output on discharge is an external electronic current I at a voltage V for a time Δt.  The chem. reaction of a rechargeable battery must be reversible on the application of a charging I and V.  Crit. parameters of a rechargeable battery are safety, d. of energy that can be stored at a specific power input and retrieved at a specific power output, cycle and shelf life, storage efficiency, and cost of fabrication.  Conventional ambient-temp. rechargeable batteries have solid electrodes and a liq. electrolyte.  The pos. electrode (cathode) consists of a host framework into which the mobile (working) cation is inserted reversibly over a finite solid-soln. range.  The solid-soln. range, which is reduced at higher current by the rate of transfer of the working ion across electrode/electrolyte interfaces and within a host, limits the amt. of charge per electrode formula unit that can be transferred over the time Δt = Δt(I).  Moreover, the difference between energies of the LUMO and the HOMO of the electrolyte, i.e., electrolyte window, dets. the max. voltage for a long shelf and cycle life.  The max. stable voltage with an aq. electrolyte is 1.5 V; the Li-ion rechargeable battery uses an org. electrolyte with a larger window, which increase the d. of stored energy for a given Δt.  Anode or cathode electrochem. potentials outside the electrolyte window can increase V, but they require formation of a passivating surface layer that must be permeable to Li+ and capable of adapting rapidly to the changing electrode surface area as the electrode changes vol. during cycling.  A passivating surface layer adds to the impedance of the Li+ transfer across the electrode/electrolyte interface and lowers the cycle life of a battery cell.  Moreover, formation of a passivation layer on the anode robs Li from the cathode irreversibly on an initial charge, further lowering the reversible Δt.  These problems plus the cost of quality control of manufg. plague development of Li-ion rechargeable batteries that can compete with the internal combustion engine for powering elec. cars and that can provide the needed low-cost storage of elec. energy generated by renewable wind and/or solar energy.  Chemists are contributing to incremental improvements of the conventional strategy by investigating and controlling electrode passivation layers, improving the rate of Li+ transfer across electrode/electrolyte interfaces, identifying electrolytes with larger windows while retaining a Li+ cond. σLi &gt; 10-3 S cm-1, synthesizing electrode morphologies that reduce the size of the active particles while pinning them on current collectors of large surface area accessible by the electrolyte, lowering the cost of cell fabrication, designing displacement-reaction anodes of higher capacity that allow a safe, fast charge, and designing alternative cathode hosts.  However, new strategies are needed for batteries that go beyond powering hand-held devices, such as using electrode hosts with two-electron redox centers; replacing the cathode hosts by materials that undergo displacement reactions (e.g. sulfur) by liq. cathodes that may contain flow-through redox mols., or by catalysts for air cathodes; and developing a Li+ solid electrolyte separator membrane that allows an org. and aq. liq. electrolyte on the anode and cathode sides, resp.  Opportunities exist for the chemist to bring together oxide and polymer or graphene chem. in imaginative morphologies.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref8" class="rightTabRefNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit8" data-doi="10.1021/nl302618s"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cao, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jeong, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cho, J.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nano Lett.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2012</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">12</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">4988</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">4991</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/nl302618s</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Spindle-like Mesoporous α-Fe2O3 Anode Material Prepared from MOF Template for High-Rate Lithium Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu, Xiaodong; Cao, Ruiguo; Jeong, Sookyung; Cho, Jaephil</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>

                        rightTab-cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Crystallographic-plane tuned Prussian-blue wrapped with RGO: a high-capacity, long-life cathode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Hui; Wang, Li; Chen, Shuangming; Li, Guopeng; Quan, Junjie; Xu, Enze; Song, Li; Jiang, Yang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3569-3577</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Designing Prussian blue with optimally exposed crystal planes and confining it in a conductive matrix are crit. issues for improving its sodium storage performance, and will result in much improved sodium ion adsorption and diffusion, together with improved electron mobility.  Here, we firstly illustrate through DFT simulations that the {100} lattice planes and [100] direction of the KxFeFe(CN)6 crystal are the preferred occupation sites and diffusion route for sodium ions.  In addn., through coupling with RGO, KxFeFe(CN)6 electrodes exhibit better electronic cond.  Accordingly, {100} plane-capped cubic K0.33FeFe(CN)6 wrapped in RGO was fabricated using a facile CTAB-assisted method.  Due to the highly robust framework, higher sp. surface area, greatly reduced no. of lattice water defects and conductive RGO coating, K0.33FeFe(CN)6/RGO exhibits superior electrochem. performance in sodium-ion batteries.  As a cathode, the RGO-coated K0.33FeFe(CN)6 yields an initial discharge-charge capacity of 160 mA h g-1 at a rate of 0.5C, and an excellent capacity retention of 92.2% at 0.5C and 90.1% at 10C after 1000 and 500 cycles.  Furthermore, x-ray diffraction, DFT simulation, XANES and EXAFS verified that the structural changes during the Na-ion insertion-extn. processes are highly reversible.  All these results suggest that {100} plane-capped K0.33FeFe(CN)6/RGO has excellent potential as a cathode for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref14" class="rightTabRefNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit14" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201105190"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Furukawa, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ohtani, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sukegawa, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nemoto, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Reboul, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kitagawa, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yamauchi, Y.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Angew.                         rightTab-cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Surface reconstruction and chemical evolution of stoichiometric layered cathode materials for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lin Feng; Doeff Marca M; Markus Isaac M; Nordlund Dennis; Weng Tsu-Chien; Asta Mark D; Xin Huolin L</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3529</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">The present study sheds light on the long-standing challenges associated with high-voltage operation of LiNi(x)Mn(x)Co(1-2x)O2 cathode materials for lithium-ion batteries.  Using correlated ensemble-averaged high-throughput X-ray absorption spectroscopy and spatially resolved electron microscopy and spectroscopy, here we report structural reconstruction (formation of a surface reduced layer, to transition) and chemical evolution (formation of a surface reaction layer) at the surface of LiNi(x)Mn(x)Co(1-2x)O2 particles.  These are primarily responsible for the prevailing capacity fading and impedance buildup under high-voltage cycling conditions, as well as the first-cycle coulombic inefficiency.  It was found that the surface reconstruction exhibits a strong anisotropic characteristic, which predominantly occurs along lithium diffusion channels.  Furthermore, the surface reaction layer is composed of lithium fluoride embedded in a complex organic matrix.  This work sets a refined example for the study of surface reconstruction and chemical evolution in battery materials using combined diagnostic tools at complementary length scales.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref22" class="rightTabRefNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit22" data-doi="10.1039/C4EE02986K"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ding, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cui, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Karpuzov, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tan, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kohandehghan, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mitlin, D.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Energy Environ.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The elec. power grid faces a growing need for large-scale energy storage over a wide range of time scales due to costly short-term transients, frequency regulation, and load balancing.  The durability, high power, energy efficiency, and low cost needed for grid-scale storage pose substantial challenges for conventional battery technol.  Here, we demonstrate insertion/extn. of sodium and potassium ions in a low-strain nickel hexacyanoferrate electrode material for at least five thousand deep cycles at high current densities in inexpensive aq. electrolytes.                             rightTab-cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref34" class="rightTabRefNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit34" data-doi="10.1038/nmat1672"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Taberna, P. L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mitra, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Poizot, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Simon, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tarascon, J. M.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nat. Mater.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2006</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">5</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">567</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">573</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1038/nmat1672</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            rightTab-cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref35" class="rightTabRefNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit35" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2015.10.029"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">An, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yoo, H. D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ru, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mai, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yao, Y.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nano Energy</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">18</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">265</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">272</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.nanoen.2015.10.029</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            rightTab-cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref36" class="rightTabRefNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit36" data-doi="10.1038/nmat2612"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Brezesinski, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tolbert, S. H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dunn, B.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nat. Mater.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2010</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">9</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">146</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">151</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1038/nmat2612</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ordered mesoporous α-MoO3 with iso-oriented nanocrystalline walls for thin-film pseudocapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Brezesinski, Torsten; Wang, John; Tolbert, Sarah H.; Dunn, Bruce</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2010</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">146-151</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NMAACR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1476-1122</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Capacitive energy storage is distinguished from other types of electrochem. energy storage by short charging times and the ability to deliver significantly more power than batteries.  A limitation to this technol. is its low energy d. and there is interest in exploring pseudo-capacitive materials where faradaic mechanisms offer increased energy storage.  The capacitive charge-storage properties of mesoporous films of iso-oriented α-MoO3 are superior to those of either mesoporous amorphous material or nonporous cryst. MoO3.  Whereas both cryst. and amorphous mesoporous materials show redox pseudo-capacitance, the iso-oriented layered cryst. domains enable Li ions to be inserted into the van der Waals gaps of the α-MoO3.  Probably this extra contribution arises from an intercalation pseudo-capacitance, which occurs on the same timescale as redox pseudo-capacitance.  The result is increased charge-storage capacity without compromising charge/discharge kinetics in mesoporous cryst. MoO3.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref37" class="rightTabRefNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit37" data-doi="10.1038/nmat3601"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Augustyn, V.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Come, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lowe, M. A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kim, J. W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Taberna, P. L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tolbert, S. H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Abruña, H. D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Simon, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dunn, B.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nat. Mater.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">12</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">518</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">522</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1038/nmat3601</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-rate electrochemical energy storage through Li+ intercalation pseudocapacitance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Augustyn, Veronica; Come, Jeremy; Lowe, Michael A.; Kim, Jong Woung; Taberna, Pierre-Louis; Tolbert, Sarah H.; Abruna, Hector D.; Simon, Patrice; Dunn, Bruce</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">518-522</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NMAACR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1476-1122</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pseudocapacitance is commonly assocd. with surface or near-surface reversible redox reactions, as obsd. with RuO2·xH2O in an acidic electrolyte.  However, we recently demonstrated that a pseudocapacitive mechanism occurs when lithium ions are inserted into mesoporous and nanocrystal films of orthorhombic Nb2O5 (T-Nb2O5; refs , ).  Here, we quantify the kinetics of charge storage in T-Nb2O5: currents that vary inversely with time, charge-storage capacity that is mostly independent of rate, and redox peaks that exhibit small voltage offsets even at high rates.  We also define the structural characteristics necessary for this process, termed intercalation pseudocapacitance, which are a cryst. network that offers two-dimensional transport pathways and little structural change on intercalation.  The principal benefit realized from intercalation pseudocapacitance is that high levels of charge storage are achieved within short periods of time because there are no limitations from solid-state diffusion.  Thick electrodes (up to 40 μm thick) prepd. with T-Nb2O5 offer the promise of exploiting intercalation pseudocapacitance to obtain high-rate charge-storage devices.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref38" class="rightTabRefNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit38" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2011.08.015"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huang, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ren, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, W.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Power Sources</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2011</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">196</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">9786</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">9791</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.jpowsour.2011.08.015</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            rightTab-cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref39" class="rightTabRefNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit39" data-doi="10.1021/ja105482k"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Matsuda, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kim, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Moritomo, Y.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Am. Chem. Soc.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2010</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">132</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">12206</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">12207</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/ja105482k</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            rightTab-cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li></ol></li><li id="pane-m3" aria-labelledby="pane-m3" class="tab__pane tab__pane-suppInfo"><h2 class="supp-info-label">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article_supporting-info" id="rightTab-notes-1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="rightTab-_i1">Supporting Information</h2></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge on the <a href="/" class="ext-link">ACS Publications website</a> at DOI: <a href="/doi/abs/10.1021/acs.nanolett.7b01366" class="ext-link">10.1021/acs.nanolett.7b01366</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">Experimental section and additional figures (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.7b01366/suppl_file/nl7b01366_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.7b01366/suppl_file/nl7b01366_si_001.pdf">nl7b01366_si_001.pdf (1.79 MB)</a></li></ul></div></div><div id="rightTab-figshare-widget"></div><br><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="b84e6b6c-b4d0-4427-b286-3cf14d52d013" class="mb-4">

(function(){
	
	/*Event Tracking for RIS menu dropdown - Article pages*/

	$('.cit-download-dropdown_button').on('click',function(e)
	{	
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':'Main'});

	});


	$('.cit-download-dropdown_content ul li').on('click',function(e)
	{	
	//	e.preventDefault();
	    var idx = $(this).index();
	    
	    var label = '';
	    if (idx === 0 ) {
	    	label = 'Citation';
	    } else if (idx === 1 ) {
	    	label = 'Abstract';
	    } else if (idx === 2 ) {
	    	label = 'Reference';
	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {
	    	label = 'More Options';
	    }
	   
	   gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':label});
	});

	$('.header_contnav-next a').on('click', function(e){
        e.preventDefault();
        gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Right Arrow'});
	}); 

 	$('.header_contnav-pre a').on('click', function(e){
	    e.preventDefault();
	     gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Left Arrow'});
	}); 

	$('.share_button').on('click', function(e){
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Share'});
	});

	$("#pane-m1con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Figures'});
	});

	$("#pane-m2con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'References'});
	});

	$("#pane-m3con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Supporting Info'});
	});

	$('.tab__close').on('click', function(){
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Close'});
	}); 



})();

</script>

<script nonce="93187fb7be29075b-MAN">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

      if (_isMobile) {
        $("#gdpr-message-modal").addClass("mobile");
      }

      var emailValid = "",
        time = 3000,
        btnStatus = true,
        errorStatus = false,
        errormessage =
          "<p class='gdpr_err'><b>Please Enter a valid email address<b><p>";

      function init() {
        setTimeout(function () {
          var cookieExist = getCookie("gdpr");
          if (cookieExist) {
            //console.log("gdpr cookie exist");
            return false;
          } else {
            //console.log("gdpr cookie does not exist")
            gdprMessage();
          }
          //Events
          $("#closebtn").on("click", hideForm);

          //Handle submit
          $("#gdpr-message-btn").on("click", function (event) {
            handleClick();
          });

          // //Hide if clicked outside div - TO DO stop handling click after submit
          // $(document).click(function(event) {
          // 	event.stopPropagation();
          //   console.log(event.target);
          //   if (!$(event.target).closest("#gdpr-message-content").length) {
          //     $("body").find("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
          //     $(this).off();
          //   }
          // });
          $("#gdpr-con-btn").click(function () {
            setCookie("gdpr", "true");
            hideForm();
          });
        }, time);
      }

      //Show the message
      function gdprMessage() {
        //console.log("Show GDPR Message");
        var tMessage, emailInput, messageButton, ewrap;

        $("#gdpr-message-modal").show();
      }

      function handleClick() {
        //console.log($("#gdpr-input").val());
        emailValid = validateEmail($("#gdpr-input").val());
        if (emailValid) {
          //Submit the form
          //Hide form
          if ($(".gdpr_err")) {
            $(".gdpr_err").hide();
          }

          $("#gdpr-message-content");
          //If successful then...
          setCookie("gdpr", "true");
          //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid + " submiting form");
        } else {
          //Show error message
          gdprErrorMessage();
          //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid);
        }
      }

      function gdprErrorMessage() {
        if (errorStatus) {
          return false;
        } else {
          errorStatus = true;
          $("#gdpr-message-content").append(errormessage);
        }
      }

      function validateEmail(email) {
        var re =
          /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
        return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
      }

      function setCookie(name, value) {
        var expires = "";
        expires = "; expires=Fri, 31 Dec 9999 23:59:59 GMT";
        document.cookie = name + "=" + (value || "") + expires + "; path=/";
      }

      function getCookie(name) {
        var match = document.cookie.match(new RegExp(name + "=([^;]+)"));
        if (match) return match[1];
      }

      function hideForm() {
        //And set cookie
        $("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
        setCookie("gdpr", "false");
        gtag("event", "GDPR Modal", {
          event_category: "Pubs GDPR",
          event_label: "GDPR Dismissal",
        });
      }

      return {
        init: init,
      };
    })();

    $(document).ready(infoCentralCapture.init);
  </script>
</p>
-->

                    
                        



        
        <script nonce="93187fb7be29075b-MAN">
var currentJournal = "Nano Letters";
$(".citationLinks > a").click(function(e){
    if($(this).text() === "ACS Full Text ") {
        gtag('event', 'ACS Full Text', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Crossref") {
        gtag('event', 'Crossref', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "CAS") {
        gtag('event', 'CAS', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "PubMed") {
        gtag('event', 'PubMed', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Google Scholar") {
        gtag('event', 'Google Scholar', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).hasClass("issue-item_open-url") === true) {
        gtag('event', 'OpenURL', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
});
</script>
